## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and concentration A, which is the fundamental problem of chemical reaction kinetics. Rate laws typically express dA/dt as functions of A (and possibly t for non-autonomous systems).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate)
- Mixed order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme/saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Competitive terms: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A) (second-order with saturation)
- Damped reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A * t (time-modulated first-order)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (general polynomial in A)
- Oscillatory forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodically driven reaction)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservation constraints → Rate expressions often include terms like (c - A) representing depletion from an initial concentration, leading to logistic or saturation forms
- Mass action kinetics → Rate is proportional to products of reactant concentrations raised to stoichiometric powers: dA/dt ~ A^n
- Equilibrium approach → Opposing terms with different signs (e.g., c0*A - c1*A^2) indicate reversible reactions approaching equilibrium
- Enzyme/catalyst saturation → Rational functions A/(c+A) or A/(c+A)^2 indicate catalytic mechanisms with finite binding sites
- Autocatalytic feedback → Products of concentration with its complement (A*(c-A)) indicate self-accelerating reactions with resource limitation
- Sequential mechanism signatures → Nested rational expressions or sums of rational terms suggest multi-step reaction mechanisms
- Induction period behavior → Explicit time dependence (t appearing in rate law) may indicate radical chain initiation or photochemical activation
- Cooperative kinetics → Hill-type expressions A^n/(c + A^n) with n>1 indicate cooperative binding or multi-molecular activation steps
